## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / mathematical biology (population dynamics ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is the time-derivative of population size P, which is the standard setup for continuous-time population dynamics. With only (t, P) available, classical models express density-independent growth, density-dependent regulation, Allee effects, harvesting, and time-varying/seasonal forcing via explicit dependence on P and/or t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Constant-rate growth: dP_dt = c0 (net constant influx/immigration minus losses, independent of P)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth/decay: dP_dt = c0 * P (per-capita rate constant; unconstrained growth or decay)
- Affine per-capita rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1) * P (effective constant per-capita growth after aggregating factors)
- Linear + quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 (crowding via negative c1; simplest density feedback beyond exponential)
- Cubic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (higher-order regulation / complex density feedback)
- Gompertz growth (continuous): dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / (P + c2)) (per-capita growth decreases logarithmically; asymmetric approach to a carrying level)
- Theta-logistic (generalized logistic family): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible curvature in density regulation via exponent c2)
- Richards growth (generalized sigmoid): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2)**c3 (extra shape parameter for sigmoids beyond theta-logistic)
- Allee effect (strong Allee, cubic form): dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (reduced growth at low P and saturation/decline at high P)
- Harvesting/removal (constant yield): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (density-regulated growth with constant catch/harvest)
- Harvesting/removal (proportional): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (density regulation plus mortality proportional to P)
- Seasonally forced growth rate: dP_dt = P * (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) (periodic environment modulating per-capita rate)
- Seasonally forced carrying effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4)) (periodic modulation of density feedback strength)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Model per-capita growth explicitly: writing (dP_dt) / (P + c0) often reveals linear, quadratic, or log dependence on P that corresponds to specific ecological mechanisms.
- Negative quadratic term in P (e.g., +c1*P**2 with c1<0) indicates simple crowding/competition; higher-order negative terms can mimic stronger-than-logistic suppression at high density.
- Logarithmic regulation (terms like P*log(c0/(P+c1))) is characteristic of Gompertz-type dynamics with slow approach and asymmetric curvature versus standard sigmoids.
- Allee effects require a low-density sign change; structurally this appears as additional factors like (c*P - 1) multiplying P, creating a threshold below which dP_dt becomes negative.
- Harvesting or constant mortality shows up as additive negative terms (e.g., -c0) or proportional losses (e.g., -c0*P), which can shift equilibria or create extinction thresholds.
- Seasonality/environmental forcing commonly appears as sinusoidal modulation of a rate or feedback term: (c0 + c1*sin(c2*t+c3)) multiplying P or P*(1-cP).
- Time-varying long-term trends (e.g., climate or management change) often map to slowly varying r(t) such as (c0 + c1*t) or (c0 + c1*exp(c2*t)) multiplying P.
- Multiple equilibria in dP_dt vs P suggests factorized polynomials in P (e.g., P*(aP-1)*(1-bP)), which directly encode equilibrium points and their stability.

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG22)

GT: c0*(c1 - exp(-c2*P))*P + c3*P*exp(-c4*t)
Candidate formulas: 54

GT (fixed):
\[
f(t,P)=0.1178160925\,(1-e^{-0.02722849124 P})P\;+\;0.1178160925\,P\,e^{-0.02722849124 t}.
\]
So GT is the sum of:
- a **P-only** part: \(0.1178160925\,P - 0.1178160925\,P e^{-kP}\) with \(k=0.02722849124\),
- plus a **separable** time-decay term: \(0.1178160925\,P e^{-k t}\).

To match GT, a candidate must be able to produce simultaneously:
1) a term \(P e^{-kP}\) with a **negative** coefficient, and
2) a term \(P e^{-k t}\),
3) and a linear \(P\) term with the right coefficient.

Also, any extra functional dependence (sin/log/rational/etc.) must be removable by setting its coefficient to 0.

---

### 1. \(P c0 + P c1 e^{Pc2} + P c3 e^{c4 t} + P c5\sin(\cdots)\)
Sin term can be killed with \(c5=0\). But exponentials are \(e^{+Pc2}\) and \(e^{+c4 t}\). We can set \(c2=-k\) and \(c4=-k\) to get decays. Then candidate has \(P c1 e^{-kP}\) and \(P c3 e^{-k t}\) and \(P c0\). However GT needs \(+0.1178P\) and \(-0.1178 P e^{-kP}\) and \(+0.1178 P e^{-kt}\). This is achievable by choosing \(c0=0.1178\), \(c1=-0.1178\), \(c2=-k\), \(c3=0.1178\), \(c4=-k\). **So this matches.**

### 2. Same as (1) but with extra \(P c5\) and sin term
Set sin coefficient \(c6=0\). Combine \(P c0 + P c5\) into one linear \(P\) coefficient by choosing \(c0+c5=0.1178\). Set \(c1=-0.1178, c2=-k, c3=0.1178, c4=-k\). **Matches.**

### 3. Extra \(c5\log(\cdot)\cos(\cdot)\)
Set \(c5=0\). Remaining is like (7): \(P c0 + P c1 e^{Pc2} + P c3 e^{c4 t}\). As in (1), choose \(c0=0.1178, c1=-0.1178, c2=-k, c3=0.1178, c4=-k\). **Matches.**

### 4. Extra constant \(c5\) and log-sin term
Set log-sin coefficient \(c6=0\) and constant \(c5=0\). Reduce to (7) and match as above. **Matches.**

### 5. Has \(P c3\sin(\cdot)\) and \(P c6 e^{c7 t}\) plus extra linear/constant
Kill sine with \(c3=0\), kill constant with \(c9=0\). Then you still need both \(P e^{-kP}\) and \(P e^{-kt}\). You have \(P c1 e^{Pc2}\) (can make \(e^{-kP}\)) and \(P c6 e^{c7 t}\) (can make \(e^{-kt}\)). Linear \(P\) can be formed from \(P c0 + P c8\). So choose \(c2=-k\), \(c1=-0.1178\); \(c7=-k\), \(c6=0.1178\); \(c0+c8=0.1178\). **Matches.**

### 6. Extra \(P c5\) and \(P^{c6}c7\sin(\cdot)\)
Set the sine term to 0 by \(c7=0\). Then it’s (8) essentially; can match by adjusting linear coefficient and exponentials as in (2). **Matches.**

### 7. \(P c0 + P c1 e^{Pc2} + P c3 e^{c4 t}\)
Directly can represent the three needed terms by choosing:
- \(c0=0.1178160925\),
- \(c1=-0.1178160925\), \(c2=-0.02722849124\),
- \(c3=0.1178160925\), \(c4=-0.02722849124\).
**Matches.**

### 8. Same as (7) plus \(P c5\)
Absorb into linear term: set \(c0+c5=0.1178\) and set the exponential parameters as in (7). **Matches.**

### 9. Same as (8) plus another linear \(P c6\)
Absorb: \(c0+c5+c6=0.1178\), and set exponentials as in (7). **Matches.**

### 10. Extra \(P^{c5}c6\sin(\cdot)+c9\)
Set \(c6=0\) to remove sine term and \(c9=0\). Reduce to (7) and match. **Matches.**

### 11. Same as (8) plus constant \(c6\)
GT has no additive constant independent of \(P\), so must set \(c6=0\). Then reduce to (8) and match. **Matches.**

### 12. Same as (7) plus constant \(c5\)
Set \(c5=0\). Reduce to (7) and match. **Matches.**

### 13. Extra \(c5(c6|P|+1)^{c7}\)
To avoid non-GT \(|P|\) dependence, set \(c5=0\). Reduce to (7) and match. **Matches.**

### 14. Contains \(P c0/(P+c1)\) and other non-GT structures
Even if you kill the \(P^{c6}c7 e^{Pc8}\) term by \(c7=0\) and set \(c4\) term to match \(P e^{-kt}\), you still have \(P c0/(P+c1)\) which cannot equal a pure linear \(P\) term for all \(P\) unless \(c0=0\) (then it vanishes). If \(c0=0\), you lose needed linear \(P\) contribution but could try to recreate it via \(P c2 + P c3\). That part is fine. Then you still need the \(-P e^{-kP}\) term: but the only \(P\)-exponential available is in \(P^{c6}c7 e^{Pc8}\), which we set to 0; if we keep it, it’s multiplied by \(P^{c6}\) and cannot be forced to be exactly \(P e^{-kP}\) unless \(c6=1\) and then it becomes \(P c7 e^{Pc8}\), which could match. However the rational term must be removed (set \(c0=0\)). Then we can set:
- \(c2+c3 = 0.1178\),
- \(c6=1, c7=-0.1178, c8=-k\),
- \(c4=0.1178, c5=-k\),
- \(c9=0\).
This actually reproduces GT (rational term gone). **Matches.**
